[**Female First Name (un) **] Serratia, Klebsiella and Staphylococcus epidermidis,

would increase the risk of infection greatly.  Over the last
few days the patient admits to increased fatigue and
somnolence and lowgrade temperatures, but denies high fevers,
rigors, purulence, erythema, or tenderness to the left
femoral site.  The patient was taken by Interventional

placed but it was noted that the internal jugular vein was
occluded.  Interventional Radiology performed a high right
internal jugular stick and started TPA infusion with the hope of

[**3095-4-10**] and subsequent removal of the patient's

     CLINICAL HISTORY: 25 year old female with history of short gut syndrome and
     TPN dependency with poor IV access. The study was initially planned to be a
     tunneled right IJ central venous catheter.
     
     RADIOLOGISTS: [**First Name4 (NamePattern1) 127**] [**Last Name (NamePattern1) 2500**] and [**First Name4 (NamePattern1) 131**] [**Last Name (NamePattern1) 126**], Dr. [**First Name (STitle) 126**] being the attending
     radiologist who was present throughout the entire procedure.
     
     PROCEDURE: The benefits and risks of the procedure were explained to the
     patient and signed written consent was obtained. The patient's right neck was
     prepped and draped in the usual sterile fashion and the anesthesiologist
     provided sedation throughout the procedure. Given the patient's known history
     of poor IV access, ultrasound guidance was used to identify the right internal
     jugular vein. The limited ultrasound revealed a thickened and irregular wall
     of the internal jugular vein above a patent superior vena cava stent. On
     ultrasound, the stent was found to be patent. A transverse cervical collateral
     was noted. A micropuncture set was used to access the high right internal
     jugular vein under ultrasound visualization very high in the neck above at the
     level of this collateral where there was still patent lumen of the jugular
     vein. A .018 guidewire was placed through the 21 gauge needle and did not pass
     freely into the stented SVC. The 21 gauge needle was replaced for the 3 french
     inner dilator from the micropuncture set. The .018 guidewire was then replaced
     for an SV 8 wire which too did not pass into the SVC as seen under
     fluoroscopic visualization. The 3 french inner dilator was then removed and
     replaced with the 4.5 french dilator from the micropuncture set and this was
     used to place a .035 [**Doctor Last Name 133**] wire. Again, under fluoroscopic guidance, the [**Doctor Last Name 133**]
     wire could not be passed into the SVC due to obstructing clot. A 4 french
     sheath was then positioned using the [**Doctor Last Name 133**] guidewire and a 4 french Cobra with
     a superstiff glidewire was advanced under fluoroscopic guidance and this was
     successfully passed through the obstructing clot through the stented SVC into
     the right atrium.
     
     Contrast was injected and a venogram demonstrated a narrowed irregular mid to
     lower internal jugular vein which was normal in appearance above a
     transcervical collateral. Patency within the SVC stent was confirmed. The
     decision was made to hold off on placement of a tunneled central line as
     originally planned and instead to infuse TPN into the IVC in an attempt to
     dissolve clot and improve patency. A 40 cm 4 french MTI sidehole infusion
     catheter (sidehole length 5 cm) was placed over the guidewire after removal of
     the Cobra catheter with the sideholes positioned in the lower internal jugular
     vein. The guidewire was removed and the effusion catheter was afixed with a
     stat lock and multiple steri-strips and occlusive dressing. An infusion of TPA

                                     FINAL REPORT
     to past infection she had removal of her right internal jugular catheter.
     Lysis of the occluded right internal jugular vein had been tried a week
     before.  The initial goal was to recannulate the IJ and place a stent for
     future access.
     
     PROCEDURE: The right chest wall and right neck were prepped in sterile
     fashion. The left groin region over the indwelling left transfemoral central
     line was also prepped in sterile fashion.  The procedure was performed under
     anesthesia. The procedure was performed by Dr. [**Last Name (STitle) **] [**Last Name (STitle) **] Dr. [**First Name (STitle) 126**] with Dr. [**First Name (STitle) 126**]
     being present throughout.
     
     The left sided femoral line was pulled partially out of the skin.  It was cut.
     Over an Amplatz glidewire exchange was made for a 10 french, 40 cm bright
     tipped sheath.  Since the goal was to dilate the internal jugular vein with a
     cutting balloon an 8 french guiding catheter with a coaxially loaded
     headhunter catheter were advanced over the glidewire into the right
     brachiocephalic stent.  There was a firm occlusion at the upper end of the
     stent.  With the glidewire it was possible to gain entry into the markedly
     scarred right internal jugular vein.  A venogram of the jugular vein was
     performed.  It demonstrated that there was basically absent flow in this
     vessel which was entirely static.
     
     In the attempt to find another free piece of that vein ultrasound was used.
     With ultrasound it was possible to see the markedly thickened wall of the
     internal jugular vein.  There was a minimum amount of potential flow artifact
     in this vessel.  Under ultrasonographic guidance a 21 gauge needle was
     advanced into this vessel and an 0.018 guidewire was advanced.  This
     demonstrated however that it was basically meetings the area recanalized from
     inferior and that also from here no flow could be observed.  Since it was not
     possible to regain entry into a patent vessel a decision was made to advance
     in this access.
     
     During probing in the stent it became obvious there was still inflow from the
     right subclavian vein.  Therefore ultrasound was used and the right subclavian
     vein was identified.  It was entered with a micropuncture needle under
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**3095-4-25**] 1:43 PM
     HICK LINE PLACE                                                 Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 14988**]
     Reason: SHORT GUT SYNDROME
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 30CC
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     ultrasonographic guidance.  An 0.018 guidewire entered through the stent.
     Since there was concern that it would not provide enough stiffness the
     decision was made to stiffen it with a snare.  From the left transfemoral
     access a 15 mm Amplatz snare was advanced into the right brachiocephalic
     stent.  In a foreign body retrieval maneuver the tip of the 0.018 guidewire
     was snared.  With this arrangement it was possible to advance a 4.5 french
     micropuncture system through the subclavian vein.  Then a 260 cm long exchange
     wire was advanced through the outer sheath part of the micropuncture set and
     was brought out in a through-and-through maneuver via the left groin.  The
     tract was then dilated first to 10 french and a 10 french peel-away sheath was
     placed.
     
     Preparations were made for tunnelling of the right chest wall.  At a site that
     the patient had located previously local anesthesia was placed for the exit
     site of the catheter.  An incision was made and a connection between the exit
     site and the subclavian puncture site was created after blunt dissection of
     the subclavian site and passage of a blunt [**Last Name (un) 56**] needle.  Over an 0.038
     guidewire a 10 french peel-away sheath was placed.  A double lumen [**Doctor Last Name 14414**]
     catheter was advanced through the tunnel and the cuff was placed in the mid
     level of the tunnel.  The catheter was then cut with fluoroscopic correlation
     so that its tip would end up in the cavoatrial junction.  Attempts to pass the
     tip of the catheter through the peel-away sheath failed since it kinked at the
     entry site into the stent.  Since also the dilator would not pass again, a 4
     french catheter with an 0.035 glidewire was used to gain access again into the
     brachiocephalic vein.  It was snared again with the Amplatz snare and brought
     out through the left femoral access.  Exchange was then made over the system
     for a 260 cm long exchange wire.  Then a 12 cm peel- away sheath was placed
     under the hope that leaving this guidewire for straightening it would be
     possible to advance the 10 french [**Doctor Last Name 14414**] next to it. This turned out to be
     possible.  The peel-away sheath was removed.  A good position was achieved
     with the tip at the cavoatrial junction and final adjustment was done under
     fluoroscopy.  The guidewire was removed.  The neck site was rinsed with
     hydrogen peroxide.  Closure over the subclavian site was performed with
     Dermabond.  The eixt site of the catheter was closed with a 20 Vicryl suture.
     The final chest radiograph was obtained.  It demonstrated the catheter in good
     location at the cavoatrial junction, ready for use. There was no pneumothorax.
     There are still some patchy infiltrates in the right lung that are known and
     are currently investigated medically.
     
     The femoral line was removed and hemostasis was achieved.  There were no
     immediate complications.
     
     IMPRESSION: Placement of a right subclavian line through the brachiocephalic
     stent with tip at the cavoatrial junction.  Completely static right internal
     jugular vein that was not amenable to recanalization (including maneuvers such
     as use of glidewires and even an 0.014 fine wire).

     * C1769 GUID WIRES INCL INF            C1769 GUID WIRES INCL INF           *
     * C1773 SNARE-RETRIEVAL DEVICE INSERT  C1894 INT.SHTH NOT/GUID,EP,NONLASER *
     * C1894 INT.SHTH NOT/GUID,EP,NONLASER  C1894 INT.SHTH NOT/GUID,EP,NONLASER *
     * C1894 INT.SHTH NOT/GUID,EP,NONLASER  C1894 INT.SHTH NOT/GUID,EP,NONLASER *
     ****************************************************************************
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     to past infection she had removal of her right internal jugular catheter.
     Lysis of the occluded right internal jugular vein had been tried a week
     before.  The initial goal was to recannulate the IJ and place a stent for
     future access.
     
     PROCEDURE: The right chest wall and right neck were prepped in sterile
     fashion. The left groin region over the indwelling left transfemoral central
     line was also prepped in sterile fashion.  The procedure was performed under
     anesthesia. The procedure was performed by Dr. [**Last Name (STitle) **] [**Last Name (STitle) **] Dr. [**First Name (STitle) 126**] with Dr. [**First Name (STitle) 126**]
     being present throughout.
     
     The left sided femoral line was pulled partially out of the skin.  It was cut.
     Over an Amplatz glidewire exchange was made for a 10 french, 40 cm bright
     tipped sheath.  Since the goal was to dilate the internal jugular vein with a
     cutting balloon an 8 french guiding catheter with a coaxially loaded
     headhunter catheter were advanced over the glidewire into the right
     brachiocephalic stent.  There was a firm occlusion at the upper end of the
     stent.  With the glidewire it was possible to gain entry into the markedly
     scarred right internal jugular vein.  A venogram of the jugular vein was
     performed.  It demonstrated that there was basically absent flow in this
     vessel which was entirely static.
     
     In the attempt to find another free piece of that vein ultrasound was used.
     With ultrasound it was possible to see the markedly thickened wall of the
     internal jugular vein.  There was a minimum amount of potential flow artifact
     in this vessel.  Under ultrasonographic guidance a 21 gauge needle was
     advanced into this vessel and an 0.018 guidewire was advanced.  This
     demonstrated however that it was basically meetings the area recanalized from
     inferior and that also from here no flow could be observed.  Since it was not
     possible to regain entry into a patent vessel a decision was made to advance
     in this access.
     
     During probing in the stent it became obvious there was still inflow from the
     right subclavian vein.  Therefore ultrasound was used and the right subclavian
     vein was identified.  It was entered with a micropuncture needle under
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**3095-4-25**] 1:43 PM
     HICK LINE PLACE                                                 Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 14988**]
     Reason: SHORT GUT SYNDROME
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 30CC
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     ultrasonographic guidance.  An 0.018 guidewire entered through the stent.
     Since there was concern that it would not provide enough stiffness the
     decision was made to stiffen it with a snare.  From the left transfemoral
     access a 15 mm Amplatz snare was advanced into the right brachiocephalic
     stent.  In a foreign body retrieval maneuver the tip of the 0.018 guidewire
     was snared.  With this arrangement it was possible to advance a 4.5 french
     micropuncture system through the subclavian vein.  Then a 260 cm long exchange
     wire was advanced through the outer sheath part of the micropuncture set and
     was brought out in a through-and-through maneuver via the left groin.  The
     tract was then dilated first to 10 french and a 10 french peel-away sheath was
     placed.
     
     Preparations were made for tunnelling of the right chest wall.  At a site that
     the patient had located previously local anesthesia was placed for the exit
     site of the catheter.  An incision was made and a connection between the exit
     site and the subclavian puncture site was created after blunt dissection of
     the subclavian site and passage of a blunt [**Last Name (un) 56**] needle.  Over an 0.038
     guidewire a 10 french peel-away sheath was placed.  A double lumen [**Doctor Last Name 14414**]
     catheter was advanced through the tunnel and the cuff was placed in the mid
     level of the tunnel.  The catheter was then cut with fluoroscopic correlation
     so that its tip would end up in the cavoatrial junction.  Attempts to pass the
     tip of the catheter through the peel-away sheath failed since it kinked at the
     entry site into the stent.  Since also the dilator would not pass again, a 4
     french catheter with an 0.035 glidewire was used to gain access again into the
     brachiocephalic vein.  It was snared again with the Amplatz snare and brought
     out through the left femoral access.  Exchange was then made over the system
     for a 260 cm long exchange wire.  Then a 12 cm peel- away sheath was placed
     under the hope that leaving this guidewire for straightening it would be
     possible to advance the 10 french [**Doctor Last Name 14414**] next to it. This turned out to be
     possible.  The peel-away sheath was removed.  A good position was achieved
     with the tip at the cavoatrial junction and final adjustment was done under
     fluoroscopy.  The guidewire was removed.  The neck site was rinsed with
     hydrogen peroxide.  Closure over the subclavian site was performed with
     Dermabond.  The eixt site of the catheter was closed with a 20 Vicryl suture.
     The final chest radiograph was obtained.  It demonstrated the catheter in good
     location at the cavoatrial junction, ready for use. There was no pneumothorax.
     There are still some patchy infiltrates in the right lung that are known and
     are currently investigated medically.
     
     The femoral line was removed and hemostasis was achieved.  There were no
     immediate complications.
     
     IMPRESSION: Placement of a right subclavian line through the brachiocephalic
     stent with tip at the cavoatrial junction.  Completely static right internal
     jugular vein that was not amenable to recanalization (including maneuvers such
     as use of glidewires and even an 0.014 fine wire).
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**3095-4-25**] 1:43 PM
     HICK LINE PLACE                                                 Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 14988**]
     Reason: SHORT GUT SYNDROME
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 30CC
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)

     jugular vein that was not amenable to recanalization (including maneuvers such
     as use of glidewires and even an 0.014 fine wire).

     HICK LINE PLACE                                                 Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 14988**]

      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 30CC

     * C1769 GUID WIRES INCL INF            C1769 GUID WIRES INCL INF           *
     * C1773 SNARE-RETRIEVAL DEVICE INSERT  C1894 INT.SHTH NOT/GUID,EP,NONLASER *
     * C1894 INT.SHTH NOT/GUID,EP,NONLASER  C1894 INT.SHTH NOT/GUID,EP,NONLASER *
     * C1894 INT.SHTH NOT/GUID,EP,NONLASER  C1894 INT.SHTH NOT/GUID,EP,NONLASER *
     ****************************************************************************
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     to past infection she had removal of her right internal jugular catheter.
     Lysis of the occluded right internal jugular vein had been tried a week
     before.  The initial goal was to recannulate the IJ and place a stent for
     future access.
     
     PROCEDURE: The right chest wall and right neck were prepped in sterile
     fashion. The left groin region over the indwelling left transfemoral central
     line was also prepped in sterile fashion.  The procedure was performed under
     anesthesia. The procedure was performed by Dr. [**Last Name (STitle) **] [**Last Name (STitle) **] Dr. [**First Name (STitle) 126**] with Dr. [**First Name (STitle) 126**]
     being present throughout.
     
     The left sided femoral line was pulled partially out of the skin.  It was cut.
     Over an Amplatz glidewire exchange was made for a 10 french, 40 cm bright
     tipped sheath.  Since the goal was to dilate the internal jugular vein with a
     cutting balloon an 8 french guiding catheter with a coaxially loaded
     headhunter catheter were advanced over the glidewire into the right
     brachiocephalic stent.  There was a firm occlusion at the upper end of the
     stent.  With the glidewire it was possible to gain entry into the markedly
     scarred right internal jugular vein.  A venogram of the jugular vein was
     performed.  It demonstrated that there was basically absent flow in this
     vessel which was entirely static.
     
     In the attempt to find another free piece of that vein ultrasound was used.
     With ultrasound it was possible to see the markedly thickened wall of the
     internal jugular vein.  There was a minimum amount of potential flow artifact
     in this vessel.  Under ultrasonographic guidance a 21 gauge needle was
     advanced into this vessel and an 0.018 guidewire was advanced.  This
     demonstrated however that it was basically meetings the area recanalized from
     inferior and that also from here no flow could be observed.  Since it was not
     possible to regain entry into a patent vessel a decision was made to advance
     in this access.
     
     During probing in the stent it became obvious there was still inflow from the
     right subclavian vein.  Therefore ultrasound was used and the right subclavian
     vein was identified.  It was entered with a micropuncture needle under
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**3095-4-25**] 1:43 PM
     HICK LINE PLACE                                                 Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 14988**]
     Reason: SHORT GUT SYNDROME
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 30CC
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     ultrasonographic guidance.  An 0.018 guidewire entered through the stent.
     Since there was concern that it would not provide enough stiffness the
     decision was made to stiffen it with a snare.  From the left transfemoral
     access a 15 mm Amplatz snare was advanced into the right brachiocephalic
     stent.  In a foreign body retrieval maneuver the tip of the 0.018 guidewire
     was snared.  With this arrangement it was possible to advance a 4.5 french
     micropuncture system through the subclavian vein.  Then a 260 cm long exchange
     wire was advanced through the outer sheath part of the micropuncture set and
     was brought out in a through-and-through maneuver via the left groin.  The
     tract was then dilated first to 10 french and a 10 french peel-away sheath was
     placed.
     
     Preparations were made for tunnelling of the right chest wall.  At a site that
     the patient had located previously local anesthesia was placed for the exit
     site of the catheter.  An incision was made and a connection between the exit
     site and the subclavian puncture site was created after blunt dissection of
     the subclavian site and passage of a blunt [**Last Name (un) 56**] needle.  Over an 0.038
     guidewire a 10 french peel-away sheath was placed.  A double lumen [**Doctor Last Name 14414**]
     catheter was advanced through the tunnel and the cuff was placed in the mid
     level of the tunnel.  The catheter was then cut with fluoroscopic correlation
     so that its tip would end up in the cavoatrial junction.  Attempts to pass the
     tip of the catheter through the peel-away sheath failed since it kinked at the
     entry site into the stent.  Since also the dilator would not pass again, a 4
     french catheter with an 0.035 glidewire was used to gain access again into the
     brachiocephalic vein.  It was snared again with the Amplatz snare and brought
     out through the left femoral access.  Exchange was then made over the system
     for a 260 cm long exchange wire.  Then a 12 cm peel- away sheath was placed
     under the hope that leaving this guidewire for straightening it would be
     possible to advance the 10 french [**Doctor Last Name 14414**] next to it. This turned out to be
     possible.  The peel-away sheath was removed.  A good position was achieved
     with the tip at the cavoatrial junction and final adjustment was done under
     fluoroscopy.  The guidewire was removed.  The neck site was rinsed with
     hydrogen peroxide.  Closure over the subclavian site was performed with
     Dermabond.  The eixt site of the catheter was closed with a 20 Vicryl suture.
     The final chest radiograph was obtained.  It demonstrated the catheter in good
     location at the cavoatrial junction, ready for use. There was no pneumothorax.
     There are still some patchy infiltrates in the right lung that are known and
     are currently investigated medically.
     
     The femoral line was removed and hemostasis was achieved.  There were no
     immediate complications.
     
     IMPRESSION: Placement of a right subclavian line through the brachiocephalic
     stent with tip at the cavoatrial junction.  Completely static right internal
     jugular vein that was not amenable to recanalization (including maneuvers such
     as use of glidewires and even an 0.014 fine wire).
                                                                 (Over)

     HICK LINE PLACE                                                 Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 14988**]

      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 30CC

     for a 260 cm long exchange wire.  Then a 12 cm peel- away sheath was placed
     under the hope that leaving this guidewire for straightening it would be
     possible to advance the 10 french [**Doctor Last Name 14414**] next to it. This turned out to be
     possible.  The peel-away sheath was removed.  A good position was achieved
     with the tip at the cavoatrial junction and final adjustment was done under
     fluoroscopy.  The guidewire was removed.  The neck site was rinsed with
     hydrogen peroxide.  Closure over the subclavian site was performed with
     Dermabond.  The eixt site of the catheter was closed with a 20 Vicryl suture.
     The final chest radiograph was obtained.  It demonstrated the catheter in good
     location at the cavoatrial junction, ready for use. There was no pneumothorax.
     There are still some patchy infiltrates in the right lung that are known and
     are currently investigated medically.
     
     The femoral line was removed and hemostasis was achieved.  There were no
     immediate complications.
     
     IMPRESSION: Placement of a right subclavian line through the brachiocephalic
     stent with tip at the cavoatrial junction.  Completely static right internal
     jugular vein that was not amenable to recanalization (including maneuvers such
     as use of glidewires and even an 0.014 fine wire).
                                                                 (Over)

      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 30CC

     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     to past infection she had removal of her right internal jugular catheter.
     Lysis of the occluded right internal jugular vein had been tried a week
     before.  The initial goal was to recannulate the IJ and place a stent for
     future access.
     
     PROCEDURE: The right chest wall and right neck were prepped in sterile
     fashion. The left groin region over the indwelling left transfemoral central
     line was also prepped in sterile fashion.  The procedure was performed under
     anesthesia. The procedure was performed by Dr. [**Last Name (STitle) **] [**Last Name (STitle) **] Dr. [**First Name (STitle) 126**] with Dr. [**First Name (STitle) 126**]
     being present throughout.
     
     The left sided femoral line was pulled partially out of the skin.  It was cut.
     Over an Amplatz glidewire exchange was made for a 10 french, 40 cm bright
     tipped sheath.  Since the goal was to dilate the internal jugular vein with a
     cutting balloon an 8 french guiding catheter with a coaxially loaded
     headhunter catheter were advanced over the glidewire into the right
     brachiocephalic stent.  There was a firm occlusion at the upper end of the
     stent.  With the glidewire it was possible to gain entry into the markedly
     scarred right internal jugular vein.  A venogram of the jugular vein was
     performed.  It demonstrated that there was basically absent flow in this
     vessel which was entirely static.
     
     In the attempt to find another free piece of that vein ultrasound was used.
     With ultrasound it was possible to see the markedly thickened wall of the
     internal jugular vein.  There was a minimum amount of potential flow artifact
     in this vessel.  Under ultrasonographic guidance a 21 gauge needle was
     advanced into this vessel and an 0.018 guidewire was advanced.  This
     demonstrated however that it was basically meetings the area recanalized from
     inferior and that also from here no flow could be observed.  Since it was not
     possible to regain entry into a patent vessel a decision was made to advance
     in this access.
     
     During probing in the stent it became obvious there was still inflow from the
     right subclavian vein.  Therefore ultrasound was used and the right subclavian
     vein was identified.  It was entered with a micropuncture needle under
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**3095-4-25**] 1:43 PM
     HICK LINE PLACE                                                 Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 14988**]
     Reason: SHORT GUT SYNDROME
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 30CC
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     ultrasonographic guidance.  An 0.018 guidewire entered through the stent.
     Since there was concern that it would not provide enough stiffness the
     decision was made to stiffen it with a snare.  From the left transfemoral
     access a 15 mm Amplatz snare was advanced into the right brachiocephalic
     stent.  In a foreign body retrieval maneuver the tip of the 0.018 guidewire
     was snared.  With this arrangement it was possible to advance a 4.5 french
     micropuncture system through the subclavian vein.  Then a 260 cm long exchange
     wire was advanced through the outer sheath part of the micropuncture set and
     was brought out in a through-and-through maneuver via the left groin.  The
     tract was then dilated first to 10 french and a 10 french peel-away sheath was
     placed.
     
     Preparations were made for tunnelling of the right chest wall.  At a site that
     the patient had located previously local anesthesia was placed for the exit
     site of the catheter.  An incision was made and a connection between the exit
     site and the subclavian puncture site was created after blunt dissection of
     the subclavian site and passage of a blunt [**Last Name (un) 56**] needle.  Over an 0.038
     guidewire a 10 french peel-away sheath was placed.  A double lumen [**Doctor Last Name 14414**]
     catheter was advanced through the tunnel and the cuff was placed in the mid
     level of the tunnel.  The catheter was then cut with fluoroscopic correlation
     so that its tip would end up in the cavoatrial junction.  Attempts to pass the
     tip of the catheter through the peel-away sheath failed since it kinked at the
     entry site into the stent.  Since also the dilator would not pass again, a 4
     french catheter with an 0.035 glidewire was used to gain access again into the
     brachiocephalic vein.  It was snared again with the Amplatz snare and brought
     out through the left femoral access.  Exchange was then made over the system
     for a 260 cm long exchange wire.  Then a 12 cm peel- away sheath was placed
     under the hope that leaving this guidewire for straightening it would be
     possible to advance the 10 french [**Doctor Last Name 14414**] next to it. This turned out to be
     possible.  The peel-away sheath was removed.  A good position was achieved
     with the tip at the cavoatrial junction and final adjustment was done under
     fluoroscopy.  The guidewire was removed.  The neck site was rinsed with
     hydrogen peroxide.  Closure over the subclavian site was performed with
     Dermabond.  The eixt site of the catheter was closed with a 20 Vicryl suture.
     The final chest radiograph was obtained.  It demonstrated the catheter in good
     location at the cavoatrial junction, ready for use. There was no pneumothorax.
     There are still some patchy infiltrates in the right lung that are known and
     are currently investigated medically.
     
     The femoral line was removed and hemostasis was achieved.  There were no
     immediate complications.

     Dermabond.  The eixt site of the catheter was closed with a 20 Vicryl suture.

     location at the cavoatrial junction, ready for use. There was no pneumothorax.
     There are still some patchy infiltrates in the right lung that are known and
     are currently investigated medically.

     immediate complications.

     catheter was indwelling was now very small, and at its tip was a large
     globular thrombus, which impaired the inflow into the main internal iliac vein

     DATE: [**3095-5-22**] 7:44 AM
     IVC GRAM                                                        Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 14991**]
     Reason: central line placement for TPN. Any line.

     segment that provides outflow from the right lower extremity.  The decision
     was therefore made to proceed with thrombolytic therapy.  Since the catheter
     would only accept an 018 guide wire, such was inserted, the line was removed
     and a micropuncture 4.5 French sheath set was advanced.  After removal of the
     inner dilator, a repeat injection was performed and TPA lysis was initiated
     with an infusion of 5 mg TPA.  After this infusion, the decision was made to
     proceed with mechanical maceration of the residual clot.  A glide wire was
     advanced, which found with entry into the right internal iliac vein.  Over
     some additional collaterals it was then possible to gain access into the left-
     sided common iliac vein stent.  Since a long time we had not been able to gain
     recanalization of the right lower extremity , therefore the decision was made
     to proceed.  With anesthesia in the room the patient was now fully intubated.
     Blood was typed and crossed and brought to the room.  Over the glide wire a 12
     French sheath was placed after intermittent facial dilatation.
      The large upsizing was necessary to be able to place a stent graft in case
     dilatation of the collaterals resulted in catastrophic rupture.
     
     The glide wire in the left common iliac vein still would not permit further
     advancement of the dilators or the sheath from the right groin, a foreign body
     retrieval maneuver to provide a through-and-through access became necessary.
     
     The left groin was prepped in sterile fashion.  The left femoral vein was
     punctured with a 19-gauge needle.  Over [**Initials (NamePattern4) **] [**Last Name (NamePattern4) 193**] guide wire an 8 French
     sheath was placed.  A 15-mm Amplatz snare was advanced, with which the glide
     wire was captured, and it was brought out the left femoral vein.  Having now a
     through-and-through access permitted some further advancement of the 12 French
     sheath.  Subsequently, angioplasty was performed with a small vessel balloon.
     To be able to place an 018 guide wire, which in case of need for placement of
     a coated stent, also would need to be less than 035, a glide catheter was used
     to be advanced over the 035 through-and-through wire.  After that a 300 cm SVA
     guide wire was placed.  Over this guide wire balloon angioplasty of the
     recanalized left iliac region was performed from centrally towards distally
     with a 6 mm balloon.  A venogram with injection at the upper-most extent of
     the recanalized region showed that there was now good flow into the IVC next
     to the inflow defect through the stent from the left lower extremity, from
     which unopacified blood was flowing into the IVC.  After this initial
     dilatation, the decision was made to place a stent so that if there should be
     catastrophic bleeding, placement of a wall graft could be performed.  A 10 mm
     x 80 mm Cordis Smartstent was placed from the recanalized right pseudo-common
     iliac vein.  Then, a second stent of the same size was placed in an
     overlapping fashion to lead further into the right-sided internal iliac vein.
     A repeat venogram was performed, which demonstrated some patency through this
     area without extravasation.  The ultimate goal was still to provide direct
     connection into the IVC, and the goal would have been to provide a parallel
     system to the stent that was indwelling from the left side.  Multiple
     maneuvers were attempted to pass by the upper exent of the  stent now

     (Cont)
     projecting into the left iliac stent, using a combination of a 4 French and a
     5 French glide catheter, a stiff glide wire, a soft glide wire, a Roadrunner
     guide wire, a Sos catheter. It was possible to gain entry into the space
     around the stent in the left common iliac vein; however, the connection
     between the upper extent of the left-sided iliac stent abutting the right
     caval wall was too firm to be traversed. Therefore, the decision was made to
     stent into the left- sided 14-mm stent with the initial attempt to then later
     extend another stent from this location into the IVC, while at the same time a
     parallel stent would be placed from the left iliac system to provide catheter
     advancement from both sides. For this purpose a 40 mm stent was placed.
     
     A repeat venogram demonstrated greater inflow into the IVC; however, there was
     still a kink with tortuosity at the lower pelvic level, from which the
     catheter was inserted.  Therefore, it became necessary to extend this area
     with another 10 x 60 mm stent in an overlapping fashion.  Even after that it
     was not possible to advance the 12 French sheath, which in the meantime had
     started to kink somewhat.  An additional stent extension was therefore
     performed around the curvature of the collateral that initially connected to
     the femoral vein on the right side.  An angioplasty to 10 mm of the entire
     region was performed.  Since there was still concern for potential bleeding, a
     10 mm x 80 mm balloon was used, that then could be possibly taken for
     tamponade.  This improved the lumen; however, there was residual stenosis at
     the upper pseudo- common iliac vein.  Therefore, dilatation with a 10 x 2 mm
     balloon was performed.  After all the stents were placed, adaptation of lumen
     to the inflow in the pelvis became necessary, which was performed with a 12-mm
     balloon.
     
     Now efforts were directed towards bringing the right-sided stent component,
     which poked mildly into the left-sided 14-mm stent toward superiorly. Multiple
     attempts were made to direct it firmly upward; however, even when this was
     achieved, there was not enough stiffness to lead this stent segment clearly
     cranially.  At this time we did not desire to place a jugular approach to
     facilitate this.  A subsequent attempt was then made by pushing the stent end
     superiorly and therefore provide enough stiffness for equipment to advance
     superiorly if the inferior direction was blocked.  For this purpose, a balloon
     occlusion balloon was fully inflated and moved up within the stented region
     from the left femoral vein. However, the stent would slip off from the balloon
     and would not point upward.
      This, however, also gave a good indication that even large-bore equipment
     could be moved past the stent and at this point it may seem wiser not to
     extend the stent further cranially and end up with kissing stents within the
     already present 14-mm stent.
     
     The right-sided sheath was exchanged over [**Initials (NamePattern4) **] [**Last Name (NamePattern4) 133**] guide wire for an 8 French
     sheath.  This sheath now ended relatively easily to the stented region.  It
     was connected to a side arm.  A double-lumen PICC line was then advanced
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**3095-5-22**] 7:44 AM
     IVC GRAM                                                        Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 14991**]
     Reason: central line placement for TPN. Any line.                   
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 225CC

     (Cont)
     fluoroscopically to the IVC to be positioned at the cavoatrial junction
     through the left-sided 8 French femoral sheath.  All sheaths and catheters
     were securely fastened at the skin, and the patient was returned in stable
     condition after extubation.
     
     IMPRESSION:
     
     Reconstruction of a pseudo-right common iliac vein through collaterals that
     were dilated and stented to 10 mm. Stenting of inrernal iliac vein and its
     collaterals to provide a pseudo-external iliac vein. Stenting and dilatation
     of the collateral intervening between this area and teh external iliac vein. A

     residual clot, an additional 5 mg TPA was given and Heparin infusion was
     started for the patient.

     to the inflow in the pelvis became necessary, which was performed with a 12-mm
     balloon.
     
     Now efforts were directed towards bringing the right-sided stent component,
     which poked mildly into the left-sided 14-mm stent toward superiorly. Multiple
     attempts were made to direct it firmly upward; however, even when this was
     achieved, there was not enough stiffness to lead this stent segment clearly
     cranially.  At this time we did not desire to place a jugular approach to
     facilitate this.  A subsequent attempt was then made by pushing the stent end
     superiorly and therefore provide enough stiffness for equipment to advance
     superiorly if the inferior direction was blocked.  For this purpose, a balloon
     occlusion balloon was fully inflated and moved up within the stented region
     from the left femoral vein. However, the stent would slip off from the balloon
     and would not point upward.
      This, however, also gave a good indication that even large-bore equipment
     could be moved past the stent and at this point it may seem wiser not to
     extend the stent further cranially and end up with kissing stents within the
     already present 14-mm stent.
     
     The right-sided sheath was exchanged over [**Initials (NamePattern4) **] [**Last Name (NamePattern4) 133**] guide wire for an 8 French
     sheath.  This sheath now ended relatively easily to the stented region.  It
     was connected to a side arm.  A double-lumen PICC line was then advanced
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**3095-5-22**] 7:44 AM
     IVC GRAM                                                        Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 14991**]
     Reason: central line placement for TPN. Any line.                   
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 225CC
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     fluoroscopically to the IVC to be positioned at the cavoatrial junction
     through the left-sided 8 French femoral sheath.  All sheaths and catheters
     were securely fastened at the skin, and the patient was returned in stable
     condition after extubation.
     
     IMPRESSION:
     
     Reconstruction of a pseudo-right common iliac vein through collaterals that
     were dilated and stented to 10 mm. Stenting of inrernal iliac vein and its
     collaterals to provide a pseudo-external iliac vein. Stenting and dilatation
     of the collateral intervening between this area and teh external iliac vein. A
     final venogram demonstrated patency of the segment. Because of some mild
     residual clot, an additional 5 mg TPA was given and Heparin infusion was
     started for the patient.

     UNDERLYING MEDICAL CONDITION:
      26 year old woman with GI vasculitis, multiple line infections admitted with

     REASON FOR THIS EXAMINATION:
      central line placement for TPN. Any line.                                       
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     HISTORY:  The patient has short gut syndrome and life-long TPN dependency. She
     had multiple prior occlusions of central vessels and their reconstruction.
      Most recently a right femoral line was placed with the tip in a large pelvic
     collateral to provide transient access until another tunneled line can be
     placed.
     
     PROCEDURE:  Through the indwelling right quadruple-lumen catheter a venogram
     of the pelvis was performed.  It demonstrated that the vessel in which the
     catheter was indwelling was now very small, and at its tip was a large
     globular thrombus, which impaired the inflow into the main internal iliac vein
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**3095-5-22**] 7:44 AM
     IVC GRAM                                                        Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 14991**]
     Reason: central line placement for TPN. Any line.                   
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 225CC

                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     segment that provides outflow from the right lower extremity.  The decision
     was therefore made to proceed with thrombolytic therapy.  Since the catheter
     would only accept an 018 guide wire, such was inserted, the line was removed
     and a micropuncture 4.5 French sheath set was advanced.  After removal of the
     inner dilator, a repeat injection was performed and TPA lysis was initiated
     with an infusion of 5 mg TPA.  After this infusion, the decision was made to
     proceed with mechanical maceration of the residual clot.  A glide wire was
     advanced, which found with entry into the right internal iliac vein.  Over
     some additional collaterals it was then possible to gain access into the left-
     sided common iliac vein stent.  Since a long time we had not been able to gain
     recanalization of the right lower extremity , therefore the decision was made
     to proceed.  With anesthesia in the room the patient was now fully intubated.
     Blood was typed and crossed and brought to the room.  Over the glide wire a 12
     French sheath was placed after intermittent facial dilatation.
      The large upsizing was necessary to be able to place a stent graft in case
     dilatation of the collaterals resulted in catastrophic rupture.
     
     The glide wire in the left common iliac vein still would not permit further
     advancement of the dilators or the sheath from the right groin, a foreign body
     retrieval maneuver to provide a through-and-through access became necessary.
     
     The left groin was prepped in sterile fashion.  The left femoral vein was
     punctured with a 19-gauge needle.  Over [**Initials (NamePattern4) **] [**Last Name (NamePattern4) 193**] guide wire an 8 French
     sheath was placed.  A 15-mm Amplatz snare was advanced, with which the glide
     wire was captured, and it was brought out the left femoral vein.  Having now a
     through-and-through access permitted some further advancement of the 12 French
     sheath.  Subsequently, angioplasty was performed with a small vessel balloon.
     To be able to place an 018 guide wire, which in case of need for placement of
     a coated stent, also would need to be less than 035, a glide catheter was used
     to be advanced over the 035 through-and-through wire.  After that a 300 cm SVA
     guide wire was placed.  Over this guide wire balloon angioplasty of the
     recanalized left iliac region was performed from centrally towards distally
     with a 6 mm balloon.  A venogram with injection at the upper-most extent of
     the recanalized region showed that there was now good flow into the IVC next
     to the inflow defect through the stent from the left lower extremity, from
     which unopacified blood was flowing into the IVC.  After this initial
     dilatation, the decision was made to place a stent so that if there should be
     catastrophic bleeding, placement of a wall graft could be performed.  A 10 mm
     x 80 mm Cordis Smartstent was placed from the recanalized right pseudo-common
     iliac vein.  Then, a second stent of the same size was placed in an
     overlapping fashion to lead further into the right-sided internal iliac vein.
     A repeat venogram was performed, which demonstrated some patency through this
     area without extravasation.  The ultimate goal was still to provide direct
     connection into the IVC, and the goal would have been to provide a parallel
     system to the stent that was indwelling from the left side.  Multiple
     maneuvers were attempted to pass by the upper exent of the  stent now
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**3095-5-22**] 7:44 AM
     IVC GRAM                                                        Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 14991**]
     Reason: central line placement for TPN. Any line.                   
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 225CC
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     projecting into the left iliac stent, using a combination of a 4 French and a
     5 French glide catheter, a stiff glide wire, a soft glide wire, a Roadrunner
     guide wire, a Sos catheter. It was possible to gain entry into the space
     around the stent in the left common iliac vein; however, the connection
     between the upper extent of the left-sided iliac stent abutting the right
     caval wall was too firm to be traversed. Therefore, the decision was made to
     stent into the left- sided 14-mm stent with the initial attempt to then later
     extend another stent from this location into the IVC, while at the same time a
     parallel stent would be placed from the left iliac system to provide catheter
     advancement from both sides. For this purpose a 40 mm stent was placed.
     
     A repeat venogram demonstrated greater inflow into the IVC; however, there was
     still a kink with tortuosity at the lower pelvic level, from which the
     catheter was inserted.  Therefore, it became necessary to extend this area
     with another 10 x 60 mm stent in an overlapping fashion.  Even after that it
     was not possible to advance the 12 French sheath, which in the meantime had
     started to kink somewhat.  An additional stent extension was therefore
     performed around the curvature of the collateral that initially connected to
     the femoral vein on the right side.  An angioplasty to 10 mm of the entire
     region was performed.  Since there was still concern for potential bleeding, a
     10 mm x 80 mm balloon was used, that then could be possibly taken for
     tamponade.  This improved the lumen; however, there was residual stenosis at
     the upper pseudo- common iliac vein.  Therefore, dilatation with a 10 x 2 mm
     balloon was performed.  After all the stents were placed, adaptation of lumen
     to the inflow in the pelvis became necessary, which was performed with a 12-mm
     balloon.
     
     Now efforts were directed towards bringing the right-sided stent component,
     which poked mildly into the left-sided 14-mm stent toward superiorly. Multiple
     attempts were made to direct it firmly upward; however, even when this was
     achieved, there was not enough stiffness to lead this stent segment clearly
     cranially.  At this time we did not desire to place a jugular approach to
     facilitate this.  A subsequent attempt was then made by pushing the stent end
     superiorly and therefore provide enough stiffness for equipment to advance
     superiorly if the inferior direction was blocked.  For this purpose, a balloon
     occlusion balloon was fully inflated and moved up within the stented region
     from the left femoral vein. However, the stent would slip off from the balloon
     and would not point upward.
      This, however, also gave a good indication that even large-bore equipment
     could be moved past the stent and at this point it may seem wiser not to
     extend the stent further cranially and end up with kissing stents within the
     already present 14-mm stent.
     
     The right-sided sheath was exchanged over [**Initials (NamePattern4) **] [**Last Name (NamePattern4) 133**] guide wire for an 8 French
     sheath.  This sheath now ended relatively easily to the stented region.  It
     was connected to a side arm.  A double-lumen PICC line was then advanced
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**3095-5-22**] 7:44 AM
     IVC GRAM                                                        Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 14991**]
     Reason: central line placement for TPN. Any line.                   
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 225CC
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     fluoroscopically to the IVC to be positioned at the cavoatrial junction
     through the left-sided 8 French femoral sheath.  All sheaths and catheters
     were securely fastened at the skin, and the patient was returned in stable
     condition after extubation.
     
     IMPRESSION:
     
     Reconstruction of a pseudo-right common iliac vein through collaterals that
     were dilated and stented to 10 mm. Stenting of inrernal iliac vein and its
     collaterals to provide a pseudo-external iliac vein. Stenting and dilatation
     of the collateral intervening between this area and teh external iliac vein. A
     final venogram demonstrated patency of the segment. Because of some mild
     residual clot, an additional 5 mg TPA was given and Heparin infusion was
     started for the patient.

     to proceed.  With anesthesia in the room the patient was now fully intubated.
     Blood was typed and crossed and brought to the room.  Over the glide wire a 12
     French sheath was placed after intermittent facial dilatation.
      The large upsizing was necessary to be able to place a stent graft in case
     dilatation of the collaterals resulted in catastrophic rupture.
     
     The glide wire in the left common iliac vein still would not permit further
     advancement of the dilators or the sheath from the right groin, a foreign body
     retrieval maneuver to provide a through-and-through access became necessary.
     
     The left groin was prepped in sterile fashion.  The left femoral vein was
     punctured with a 19-gauge needle.  Over [**Initials (NamePattern4) **] [**Last Name (NamePattern4) 193**] guide wire an 8 French
     sheath was placed.  A 15-mm Amplatz snare was advanced, with which the glide
     wire was captured, and it was brought out the left femoral vein.  Having now a
     through-and-through access permitted some further advancement of the 12 French
     sheath.  Subsequently, angioplasty was performed with a small vessel balloon.
     To be able to place an 018 guide wire, which in case of need for placement of
     a coated stent, also would need to be less than 035, a glide catheter was used
     to be advanced over the 035 through-and-through wire.  After that a 300 cm SVA
     guide wire was placed.  Over this guide wire balloon angioplasty of the
     recanalized left iliac region was performed from centrally towards distally
     with a 6 mm balloon.  A venogram with injection at the upper-most extent of
     the recanalized region showed that there was now good flow into the IVC next
     to the inflow defect through the stent from the left lower extremity, from
     which unopacified blood was flowing into the IVC.  After this initial
     dilatation, the decision was made to place a stent so that if there should be
     catastrophic bleeding, placement of a wall graft could be performed.  A 10 mm
     x 80 mm Cordis Smartstent was placed from the recanalized right pseudo-common
     iliac vein.  Then, a second stent of the same size was placed in an
     overlapping fashion to lead further into the right-sided internal iliac vein.
     A repeat venogram was performed, which demonstrated some patency through this
     area without extravasation.  The ultimate goal was still to provide direct
     connection into the IVC, and the goal would have been to provide a parallel
     system to the stent that was indwelling from the left side.  Multiple
     maneuvers were attempted to pass by the upper exent of the  stent now

     IVC GRAM                                                        Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 14991**]
     Reason: central line placement for TPN. Any line.                   
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 225CC

                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     projecting into the left iliac stent, using a combination of a 4 French and a
     5 French glide catheter, a stiff glide wire, a soft glide wire, a Roadrunner
     guide wire, a Sos catheter. It was possible to gain entry into the space
     around the stent in the left common iliac vein; however, the connection
     between the upper extent of the left-sided iliac stent abutting the right
     caval wall was too firm to be traversed. Therefore, the decision was made to
     stent into the left- sided 14-mm stent with the initial attempt to then later
     extend another stent from this location into the IVC, while at the same time a
     parallel stent would be placed from the left iliac system to provide catheter
     advancement from both sides. For this purpose a 40 mm stent was placed.
     
     A repeat venogram demonstrated greater inflow into the IVC; however, there was
     still a kink with tortuosity at the lower pelvic level, from which the
     catheter was inserted.  Therefore, it became necessary to extend this area
     with another 10 x 60 mm stent in an overlapping fashion.  Even after that it
     was not possible to advance the 12 French sheath, which in the meantime had
     started to kink somewhat.  An additional stent extension was therefore
     performed around the curvature of the collateral that initially connected to
     the femoral vein on the right side.  An angioplasty to 10 mm of the entire
     region was performed.  Since there was still concern for potential bleeding, a
     10 mm x 80 mm balloon was used, that then could be possibly taken for
     tamponade.  This improved the lumen; however, there was residual stenosis at
     the upper pseudo- common iliac vein.  Therefore, dilatation with a 10 x 2 mm
     balloon was performed.  After all the stents were placed, adaptation of lumen
     to the inflow in the pelvis became necessary, which was performed with a 12-mm
     balloon.
     
     Now efforts were directed towards bringing the right-sided stent component,
     which poked mildly into the left-sided 14-mm stent toward superiorly. Multiple
     attempts were made to direct it firmly upward; however, even when this was
     achieved, there was not enough stiffness to lead this stent segment clearly
     cranially.  At this time we did not desire to place a jugular approach to
     facilitate this.  A subsequent attempt was then made by pushing the stent end
     superiorly and therefore provide enough stiffness for equipment to advance
     superiorly if the inferior direction was blocked.  For this purpose, a balloon
     occlusion balloon was fully inflated and moved up within the stented region
     from the left femoral vein. However, the stent would slip off from the balloon
     and would not point upward.
      This, however, also gave a good indication that even large-bore equipment
     could be moved past the stent and at this point it may seem wiser not to
     extend the stent further cranially and end up with kissing stents within the
     already present 14-mm stent.
     
     The right-sided sheath was exchanged over [**Initials (NamePattern4) **] [**Last Name (NamePattern4) 133**] guide wire for an 8 French
     sheath.  This sheath now ended relatively easily to the stented region.  It
     was connected to a side arm.  A double-lumen PICC line was then advanced
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**3095-5-22**] 7:44 AM
     IVC GRAM                                                        Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 14991**]
     Reason: central line placement for TPN. Any line.                   
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 225CC
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     fluoroscopically to the IVC to be positioned at the cavoatrial junction
     through the left-sided 8 French femoral sheath.  All sheaths and catheters
     were securely fastened at the skin, and the patient was returned in stable
     condition after extubation.
     
     IMPRESSION:
     
     Reconstruction of a pseudo-right common iliac vein through collaterals that
     were dilated and stented to 10 mm. Stenting of inrernal iliac vein and its
     collaterals to provide a pseudo-external iliac vein. Stenting and dilatation
     of the collateral intervening between this area and teh external iliac vein. A
     final venogram demonstrated patency of the segment. Because of some mild
     residual clot, an additional 5 mg TPA was given and Heparin infusion was
     started for the patient.

     10 mm x 80 mm balloon was used, that then could be possibly taken for
     tamponade.  This improved the lumen; however, there was residual stenosis at
     the upper pseudo- common iliac vein.  Therefore, dilatation with a 10 x 2 mm
     balloon was performed.  After all the stents were placed, adaptation of lumen
     to the inflow in the pelvis became necessary, which was performed with a 12-mm
     balloon.
     
     Now efforts were directed towards bringing the right-sided stent component,
     which poked mildly into the left-sided 14-mm stent toward superiorly. Multiple
     attempts were made to direct it firmly upward; however, even when this was
     achieved, there was not enough stiffness to lead this stent segment clearly
     cranially.  At this time we did not desire to place a jugular approach to
     facilitate this.  A subsequent attempt was then made by pushing the stent end
     superiorly and therefore provide enough stiffness for equipment to advance
     superiorly if the inferior direction was blocked.  For this purpose, a balloon
     occlusion balloon was fully inflated and moved up within the stented region
     from the left femoral vein. However, the stent would slip off from the balloon
     and would not point upward.
      This, however, also gave a good indication that even large-bore equipment
     could be moved past the stent and at this point it may seem wiser not to
     extend the stent further cranially and end up with kissing stents within the
     already present 14-mm stent.
     
     The right-sided sheath was exchanged over [**Initials (NamePattern4) **] [**Last Name (NamePattern4) 133**] guide wire for an 8 French
     sheath.  This sheath now ended relatively easily to the stented region.  It
     was connected to a side arm.  A double-lumen PICC line was then advanced
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**3095-5-22**] 7:44 AM
     IVC GRAM                                                        Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 14991**]
     Reason: central line placement for TPN. Any line.                   
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 225CC
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     fluoroscopically to the IVC to be positioned at the cavoatrial junction
     through the left-sided 8 French femoral sheath.  All sheaths and catheters
     were securely fastened at the skin, and the patient was returned in stable
     condition after extubation.
     
     IMPRESSION:
     
     Reconstruction of a pseudo-right common iliac vein through collaterals that
     were dilated and stented to 10 mm. Stenting of inrernal iliac vein and its
     collaterals to provide a pseudo-external iliac vein. Stenting and dilatation
     of the collateral intervening between this area and teh external iliac vein. A
     final venogram demonstrated patency of the segment. Because of some mild
     residual clot, an additional 5 mg TPA was given and Heparin infusion was
     started for the patient.

     UNDERLYING MEDICAL CONDITION:
      26 year old woman with GI vasculitis, multiple line infections admitted with

     REASON FOR THIS EXAMINATION:
      central line placement for TPN. Any line.                                       
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     HISTORY:  The patient has short gut syndrome and life-long TPN dependency. She
     had multiple prior occlusions of central vessels and their reconstruction.
      Most recently a right femoral line was placed with the tip in a large pelvic
     collateral to provide transient access until another tunneled line can be
     placed.
     
     PROCEDURE:  Through the indwelling right quadruple-lumen catheter a venogram
     of the pelvis was performed.  It demonstrated that the vessel in which the
     catheter was indwelling was now very small, and at its tip was a large
     globular thrombus, which impaired the inflow into the main internal iliac vein
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**3095-5-22**] 7:44 AM
     IVC GRAM                                                        Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 14991**]
     Reason: central line placement for TPN. Any line.

                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     segment that provides outflow from the right lower extremity.  The decision
     was therefore made to proceed with thrombolytic therapy.  Since the catheter
     would only accept an 018 guide wire, such was inserted, the line was removed
     and a micropuncture 4.5 French sheath set was advanced.  After removal of the
     inner dilator, a repeat injection was performed and TPA lysis was initiated
     with an infusion of 5 mg TPA.  After this infusion, the decision was made to
     proceed with mechanical maceration of the residual clot.  A glide wire was
     advanced, which found with entry into the right internal iliac vein.  Over
     some additional collaterals it was then possible to gain access into the left-
     sided common iliac vein stent.  Since a long time we had not been able to gain
     recanalization of the right lower extremity , therefore the decision was made
     to proceed.  With anesthesia in the room the patient was now fully intubated.
     Blood was typed and crossed and brought to the room.  Over the glide wire a 12
     French sheath was placed after intermittent facial dilatation.
      The large upsizing was necessary to be able to place a stent graft in case
     dilatation of the collaterals resulted in catastrophic rupture.
     
     The glide wire in the left common iliac vein still would not permit further
     advancement of the dilators or the sheath from the right groin, a foreign body
     retrieval maneuver to provide a through-and-through access became necessary.
     
     The left groin was prepped in sterile fashion.  The left femoral vein was
     punctured with a 19-gauge needle.  Over [**Initials (NamePattern4) **] [**Last Name (NamePattern4) 193**] guide wire an 8 French
     sheath was placed.  A 15-mm Amplatz snare was advanced, with which the glide
     wire was captured, and it was brought out the left femoral vein.  Having now a
     through-and-through access permitted some further advancement of the 12 French
     sheath.  Subsequently, angioplasty was performed with a small vessel balloon.
     To be able to place an 018 guide wire, which in case of need for placement of
     a coated stent, also would need to be less than 035, a glide catheter was used
     to be advanced over the 035 through-and-through wire.  After that a 300 cm SVA
     guide wire was placed.  Over this guide wire balloon angioplasty of the
     recanalized left iliac region was performed from centrally towards distally
     with a 6 mm balloon.  A venogram with injection at the upper-most extent of
     the recanalized region showed that there was now good flow into the IVC next
     to the inflow defect through the stent from the left lower extremity, from
     which unopacified blood was flowing into the IVC.  After this initial
     dilatation, the decision was made to place a stent so that if there should be
     catastrophic bleeding, placement of a wall graft could be performed.  A 10 mm
     x 80 mm Cordis Smartstent was placed from the recanalized right pseudo-common
     iliac vein.  Then, a second stent of the same size was placed in an
     overlapping fashion to lead further into the right-sided internal iliac vein.
     A repeat venogram was performed, which demonstrated some patency through this
     area without extravasation.  The ultimate goal was still to provide direct
     connection into the IVC, and the goal would have been to provide a parallel
     system to the stent that was indwelling from the left side.  Multiple
     maneuvers were attempted to pass by the upper exent of the  stent now
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**3095-5-22**] 7:44 AM
     IVC GRAM                                                        Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 14991**]
     Reason: central line placement for TPN. Any line.                   
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 225CC
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     projecting into the left iliac stent, using a combination of a 4 French and a
     5 French glide catheter, a stiff glide wire, a soft glide wire, a Roadrunner
     guide wire, a Sos catheter. It was possible to gain entry into the space
     around the stent in the left common iliac vein; however, the connection
     between the upper extent of the left-sided iliac stent abutting the right
     caval wall was too firm to be traversed. Therefore, the decision was made to
     stent into the left- sided 14-mm stent with the initial attempt to then later
     extend another stent from this location into the IVC, while at the same time a
     parallel stent would be placed from the left iliac system to provide catheter
     advancement from both sides. For this purpose a 40 mm stent was placed.
     
     A repeat venogram demonstrated greater inflow into the IVC; however, there was
     still a kink with tortuosity at the lower pelvic level, from which the
     catheter was inserted.  Therefore, it became necessary to extend this area
     with another 10 x 60 mm stent in an overlapping fashion.  Even after that it
     was not possible to advance the 12 French sheath, which in the meantime had
     started to kink somewhat.  An additional stent extension was therefore
     performed around the curvature of the collateral that initially connected to
     the femoral vein on the right side.  An angioplasty to 10 mm of the entire
     region was performed.  Since there was still concern for potential bleeding, a
     10 mm x 80 mm balloon was used, that then could be possibly taken for
     tamponade.  This improved the lumen; however, there was residual stenosis at
     the upper pseudo- common iliac vein.  Therefore, dilatation with a 10 x 2 mm
     balloon was performed.  After all the stents were placed, adaptation of lumen
     to the inflow in the pelvis became necessary, which was performed with a 12-mm
     balloon.
     
     Now efforts were directed towards bringing the right-sided stent component,
     which poked mildly into the left-sided 14-mm stent toward superiorly. Multiple
     attempts were made to direct it firmly upward; however, even when this was
     achieved, there was not enough stiffness to lead this stent segment clearly
     cranially.  At this time we did not desire to place a jugular approach to
     facilitate this.  A subsequent attempt was then made by pushing the stent end
     superiorly and therefore provide enough stiffness for equipment to advance
     superiorly if the inferior direction was blocked.  For this purpose, a balloon
     occlusion balloon was fully inflated and moved up within the stented region
     from the left femoral vein. However, the stent would slip off from the balloon
     and would not point upward.
      This, however, also gave a good indication that even large-bore equipment
     could be moved past the stent and at this point it may seem wiser not to
     extend the stent further cranially and end up with kissing stents within the
     already present 14-mm stent.
     
     The right-sided sheath was exchanged over [**Initials (NamePattern4) **] [**Last Name (NamePattern4) 133**] guide wire for an 8 French
     sheath.  This sheath now ended relatively easily to the stented region.  It
     was connected to a side arm.  A double-lumen PICC line was then advanced
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**3095-5-22**] 7:44 AM
     IVC GRAM                                                        Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 14991**]
     Reason: central line placement for TPN. Any line.                   
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 225CC
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     fluoroscopically to the IVC to be positioned at the cavoatrial junction
     through the left-sided 8 French femoral sheath.  All sheaths and catheters
     were securely fastened at the skin, and the patient was returned in stable
     condition after extubation.
     
     IMPRESSION:
     
     Reconstruction of a pseudo-right common iliac vein through collaterals that
     were dilated and stented to 10 mm. Stenting of inrernal iliac vein and its
     collaterals to provide a pseudo-external iliac vein. Stenting and dilatation
     of the collateral intervening between this area and teh external iliac vein. A
     final venogram demonstrated patency of the segment. Because of some mild
     residual clot, an additional 5 mg TPA was given and Heparin infusion was
     started for the patient.
