     segment that provides outflow from the right lower extremity.  The decision
     was therefore made to proceed with thrombolytic therapy.  Since the catheter
     would only accept an 018 guide wire, such was inserted, the line was removed
     and a micropuncture 4.5 French sheath set was advanced.  After removal of the
     inner dilator, a repeat injection was performed and TPA lysis was initiated
     with an infusion of 5 mg TPA.  After this infusion, the decision was made to
     proceed with mechanical maceration of the residual clot.  A glide wire was
     advanced, which found with entry into the right internal iliac vein.  Over
     some additional collaterals it was then possible to gain access into the left-
     sided common iliac vein stent.  Since a long time we had not been able to gain
     recanalization of the right lower extremity , therefore the decision was made
     to proceed.  With anesthesia in the room the patient was now fully intubated.
     Blood was typed and crossed and brought to the room.  Over the glide wire a 12
     French sheath was placed after intermittent facial dilatation.
      The large upsizing was necessary to be able to place a stent graft in case
     dilatation of the collaterals resulted in catastrophic rupture.
     
     The glide wire in the left common iliac vein still would not permit further
     advancement of the dilators or the sheath from the right groin, a foreign body
     retrieval maneuver to provide a through-and-through access became necessary.
     
     The left groin was prepped in sterile fashion.  The left femoral vein was
     punctured with a 19-gauge needle.  Over [**Initials (NamePattern4) **] [**Last Name (NamePattern4) 193**] guide wire an 8 French
     sheath was placed.  A 15-mm Amplatz snare was advanced, with which the glide
     wire was captured, and it was brought out the left femoral vein.  Having now a
     through-and-through access permitted some further advancement of the 12 French
     sheath.  Subsequently, angioplasty was performed with a small vessel balloon.
     To be able to place an 018 guide wire, which in case of need for placement of
     a coated stent, also would need to be less than 035, a glide catheter was used
     to be advanced over the 035 through-and-through wire.  After that a 300 cm SVA
     guide wire was placed.  Over this guide wire balloon angioplasty of the
     recanalized left iliac region was performed from centrally towards distally
     with a 6 mm balloon.  A venogram with injection at the upper-most extent of
     the recanalized region showed that there was now good flow into the IVC next
     to the inflow defect through the stent from the left lower extremity, from
     which unopacified blood was flowing into the IVC.  After this initial
     dilatation, the decision was made to place a stent so that if there should be
     catastrophic bleeding, placement of a wall graft could be performed.  A 10 mm
     x 80 mm Cordis Smartstent was placed from the recanalized right pseudo-common
     iliac vein.  Then, a second stent of the same size was placed in an
     overlapping fashion to lead further into the right-sided internal iliac vein.
     A repeat venogram was performed, which demonstrated some patency through this
     area without extravasation.  The ultimate goal was still to provide direct
     connection into the IVC, and the goal would have been to provide a parallel
     system to the stent that was indwelling from the left side.  Multiple
     maneuvers were attempted to pass by the upper exent of the  stent now
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**3095-5-22**] 7:44 AM
     IVC GRAM                                                        Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 14991**]
     Reason: central line placement for TPN. Any line.                   
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 225CC
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     projecting into the left iliac stent, using a combination of a 4 French and a
     5 French glide catheter, a stiff glide wire, a soft glide wire, a Roadrunner
     guide wire, a Sos catheter. It was possible to gain entry into the space
     around the stent in the left common iliac vein; however, the connection
     between the upper extent of the left-sided iliac stent abutting the right
     caval wall was too firm to be traversed. Therefore, the decision was made to
     stent into the left- sided 14-mm stent with the initial attempt to then later
     extend another stent from this location into the IVC, while at the same time a
     parallel stent would be placed from the left iliac system to provide catheter
     advancement from both sides. For this purpose a 40 mm stent was placed.
     
     A repeat venogram demonstrated greater inflow into the IVC; however, there was
     still a kink with tortuosity at the lower pelvic level, from which the
     catheter was inserted.  Therefore, it became necessary to extend this area
     with another 10 x 60 mm stent in an overlapping fashion.  Even after that it
     was not possible to advance the 12 French sheath, which in the meantime had
     started to kink somewhat.  An additional stent extension was therefore
     performed around the curvature of the collateral that initially connected to
     the femoral vein on the right side.  An angioplasty to 10 mm of the entire
     region was performed.  Since there was still concern for potential bleeding, a
     10 mm x 80 mm balloon was used, that then could be possibly taken for
     tamponade.  This improved the lumen; however, there was residual stenosis at
     the upper pseudo- common iliac vein.  Therefore, dilatation with a 10 x 2 mm
     balloon was performed.  After all the stents were placed, adaptation of lumen
     to the inflow in the pelvis became necessary, which was performed with a 12-mm
     balloon.
     
     Now efforts were directed towards bringing the right-sided stent component,
     which poked mildly into the left-sided 14-mm stent toward superiorly. Multiple
     attempts were made to direct it firmly upward; however, even when this was
     achieved, there was not enough stiffness to lead this stent segment clearly
     cranially.  At this time we did not desire to place a jugular approach to
     facilitate this.  A subsequent attempt was then made by pushing the stent end
     superiorly and therefore provide enough stiffness for equipment to advance
     superiorly if the inferior direction was blocked.  For this purpose, a balloon
     occlusion balloon was fully inflated and moved up within the stented region
     from the left femoral vein. However, the stent would slip off from the balloon
     and would not point upward.
      This, however, also gave a good indication that even large-bore equipment
     could be moved past the stent and at this point it may seem wiser not to
     extend the stent further cranially and end up with kissing stents within the
     already present 14-mm stent.
     
     The right-sided sheath was exchanged over [**Initials (NamePattern4) **] [**Last Name (NamePattern4) 133**] guide wire for an 8 French
     sheath.  This sheath now ended relatively easily to the stented region.  It
     was connected to a side arm.  A double-lumen PICC line was then advanced
                                                                 (Over)

     DATE: [**3095-5-22**] 7:44 AM
     IVC GRAM                                                        Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 14991**]
     Reason: central line placement for TPN. Any line.                   
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 225CC
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     fluoroscopically to the IVC to be positioned at the cavoatrial junction
     through the left-sided 8 French femoral sheath.  All sheaths and catheters
     were securely fastened at the skin, and the patient was returned in stable
     condition after extubation.
     
     IMPRESSION:
     
     Reconstruction of a pseudo-right common iliac vein through collaterals that
     were dilated and stented to 10 mm. Stenting of inrernal iliac vein and its
     collaterals to provide a pseudo-external iliac vein. Stenting and dilatation
     of the collateral intervening between this area and teh external iliac vein. A
     final venogram demonstrated patency of the segment. Because of some mild
     residual clot, an additional 5 mg TPA was given and Heparin infusion was
     started for the patient.

     superiorly if the inferior direction was blocked.  For this purpose, a balloon

     puncture needle exchanged for a 4.5 french sheath and then exchanged over a
     [**Doctor Last Name 133**] 6 and 8 mm dilators under fluoroscopic observation.  The dilator was
     then exchanged for an 8 french triple lumen central venous catheter with tip
     demonstrated to be within the right atrium.  The catheter is demonstrated to
     flush and aspirate well and is secured with 0 Prolene.  Post procedure chest
     fluoroscopy demonstrates the tip of the catheter to be within the right atrium
     and no pneumothorax is demonstrated.
     
     The left common femoral vein catheter is then withdrawn and hemostasis is
     obtained.  There were no immediate complications and the patient tolerated the
     procedure well.
     
     IMPRESSION:
     1) Extension of right iliac stent to a level just proximal to the right
     superficial femoral vein with a 12 mm x 80 mm Smart, self expandable stent
     with subsequent balloon dilatation to 10 mm.
     
     2) Good flow demonstrated within the reconstructed iliac vein and no filling
     defects suggestive of thrombus.
     
     3) Successful placement of right IJ triple lumen central venous catheter with
     tip in the right atrium.  The catheter is ready for use.

     MEDICATION AND CONTRAST: MAC was provided by the anesthesiology department.  A
     total of 5 cc 1% subcutaneous lidocaine was administered.  A total of 140 cc
     nonionc contrast were administered due to patient's generalized debilitation.
     
     PROCEDURE/TECHNIQUE:  Informed consent was obtained from patient's mother. The
     patient was placed supine on the angiographic table and bilateral groins and
     right neck were sterile prepped and draped in the usual fashion.  Through the
     previously placed right sided common femoral vein 6 french sheath an initial
     venogram was obtained and demonstrated rapid flow through the patent
     reconstructed right iliac vein with rapid flow into the inferior vena cava and
     into multiple pelvic venous collaterals.  Previously placed stents are
     demonstrated to be widely patent and no filling defects suggestive of thrombus
     were demonstrated. There was however a stenosis in the right external iliac
     vein/ femoral vein peripheral to the stent. The decision was made to
     angioplasty and stent this area. Because of the close proximity to the entry
     site an access from contralateral became necessary.
     
     The location of the proximal entry site of the right sided common femoral vein
     sheath was determied and it was decided that the approach be made from the
     contralateral, left, common femoral vein previously placed sheath.  The
     previously placed PICC line is removed.  Through the left common femoral vein
     8 french sheath [**Initials (NamePattern4) **] [**Last Name (NamePattern4) 133**] wire and C2 Cobra catheter were advanced through the
     stented left common iliac vein crossing the bifurcation and entering the right
     reconstructed stented iliac vein.  The catheter and guidewire were then
     advanced to the level of the right common femoral vein.  The catheter was then
     exchanged for a 10 mm balloon over [**Initials (NamePattern4) **] [**Last Name (NamePattern4) 133**] wire and the proximal stented
     common femoral vein is dilated again.  The right common femoral vein sheath is
     then removed and hemostasis was obtained.
                                                                 (Over)

     through the deflated ballon which was advancd into the superficial femoral

     reconstructed stented iliac vein.  The catheter and guidewire were then
     advanced to the level of the right common femoral vein.  The catheter was then
     exchanged for a 10 mm balloon over [**Initials (NamePattern4) **] [**Last Name (NamePattern4) 133**] wire and the proximal stented
     common femoral vein is dilated again.  The right common femoral vein sheath is
     then removed and hemostasis was obtained.

     DATE: [**3095-5-24**] 7:44 AM
     IVC GRAM                                                        Clip # [**Clip Number (Radiology) 14992**]
     Reason: SHORT GUT SYNDROME
      Contrast: OPTIRAY Amt: 140
     ______________________________________________________________________________
                                     FINAL REPORT
     (Cont)
     
     A 12 mm x 80 mm self expandable stent is then deployed under fluoroscopic
     observation spanning from the stented right reconstructed external iliac vein
     to the right common femoral vein, just proximal to the superficial femoral
     vein.  This stent is then dilated with a 10 mm balloon.  Subsequent venogram
     through the deflated ballon which was advancd into the superficial femoral
     vein demonstrates a widely patent stented iliac veins with good flow of
     contrast into a widely patent superficial femoral vein.  The balloon catheter
     is then withdrawn.
     
     Under ultrasonographic and fluoroscopic observation the stented superior vena
     cava is then entered using a 21 gauge micropuncture needle via the right neck.
     1% subcutaneous lidocaine was administerd prior to the access.  An 0.018
     guidewire was then advanced into the stented superior vena cava and the
     puncture needle exchanged for a 4.5 french sheath and then exchanged over a
     [**Doctor Last Name 133**] 6 and 8 mm dilators under fluoroscopic observation.  The dilator was
     then exchanged for an 8 french triple lumen central venous catheter with tip
     demonstrated to be within the right atrium.  The catheter is demonstrated to
     flush and aspirate well and is secured with 0 Prolene.  Post procedure chest
     fluoroscopy demonstrates the tip of the catheter to be within the right atrium
     and no pneumothorax is demonstrated.
     
     The left common femoral vein catheter is then withdrawn and hemostasis is
     obtained.  There were no immediate complications and the patient tolerated the
     procedure well.
     
     IMPRESSION:
     1) Extension of right iliac stent to a level just proximal to the right
     superficial femoral vein with a 12 mm x 80 mm Smart, self expandable stent
     with subsequent balloon dilatation to 10 mm.
     
     2) Good flow demonstrated within the reconstructed iliac vein and no filling
     defects suggestive of thrombus.
     
     3) Successful placement of right IJ triple lumen central venous catheter with
     tip in the right atrium.  The catheter is ready for use.

     MEDICATION AND CONTRAST: MAC was provided by the anesthesiology department.  A
     total of 5 cc 1% subcutaneous lidocaine was administered.  A total of 140 cc
     nonionc contrast were administered due to patient's generalized debilitation.
     
     PROCEDURE/TECHNIQUE:  Informed consent was obtained from patient's mother. The
     patient was placed supine on the angiographic table and bilateral groins and
     right neck were sterile prepped and draped in the usual fashion.  Through the
     previously placed right sided common femoral vein 6 french sheath an initial
     venogram was obtained and demonstrated rapid flow through the patent
     reconstructed right iliac vein with rapid flow into the inferior vena cava and
     into multiple pelvic venous collaterals.  Previously placed stents are
     demonstrated to be widely patent and no filling defects suggestive of thrombus
     were demonstrated. There was however a stenosis in the right external iliac
     vein/ femoral vein peripheral to the stent. The decision was made to
     angioplasty and stent this area. Because of the close proximity to the entry
     site an access from contralateral became necessary.
     
     The location of the proximal entry site of the right sided common femoral vein
     sheath was determied and it was decided that the approach be made from the
     contralateral, left, common femoral vein previously placed sheath.  The
     previously placed PICC line is removed.  Through the left common femoral vein
     8 french sheath [**Initials (NamePattern4) **] [**Last Name (NamePattern4) 133**] wire and C2 Cobra catheter were advanced through the
     stented left common iliac vein crossing the bifurcation and entering the right
     reconstructed stented iliac vein.  The catheter and guidewire were then
     advanced to the level of the right common femoral vein.  The catheter was then
     exchanged for a 10 mm balloon over [**Initials (NamePattern4) **] [**Last Name (NamePattern4) 133**] wire and the proximal stented
     common femoral vein is dilated again.  The right common femoral vein sheath is
     then removed and hemostasis was obtained.

     observation spanning from the stented right reconstructed external iliac vein
     to the right common femoral vein, just proximal to the superficial femoral
     vein.  This stent is then dilated with a 10 mm balloon.  Subsequent venogram
     through the deflated ballon which was advancd into the superficial femoral
     vein demonstrates a widely patent stented iliac veins with good flow of
     contrast into a widely patent superficial femoral vein.  The balloon catheter
     is then withdrawn.

     [**Doctor Last Name 133**] 6 and 8 mm dilators under fluoroscopic observation.  The dilator was
     then exchanged for an 8 french triple lumen central venous catheter with tip
     demonstrated to be within the right atrium.  The catheter is demonstrated to
     flush and aspirate well and is secured with 0 Prolene.  Post procedure chest
     fluoroscopy demonstrates the tip of the catheter to be within the right atrium
     and no pneumothorax is demonstrated.
     
     The left common femoral vein catheter is then withdrawn and hemostasis is
     obtained.  There were no immediate complications and the patient tolerated the
     procedure well.

     superficial femoral vein with a 12 mm x 80 mm Smart, self expandable stent
     with subsequent balloon dilatation to 10 mm.

     defects suggestive of thrombus.

     tip in the right atrium.  The catheter is ready for use.

                                     FINAL REPORT
     
     
     
     This is a 26 year old female who has short bowel syndrome and is in need of
     paraenteral nutrition.  A short catheter had previously been placed in the
     right internal jugular vein with the tip lying in the distal SVC for IV
     medication.  Because there was a question of infection and the patient was not
     febrile, decision as made to place a long-term tunneled catheter.
     
     Informed consent was obtained.  The right internal jugular and infraclavicular
     area was prepped with Betadine and a drape placed.  The spot for the tunnel
     was selected and a small 5 mm incision was made in the skin.  The tissues were
     spread and a tunnel was made from the infraclavicular area to the skin site
     where the previous placed catheter was placed.  A guidewire was advanced
     through the tunnel and the tunnel dilated with a peel away sheath to 9 French.
     The 7 French dual lumen Hickman with a cuff was placed in satisfactory
     position and the tunnel jugular catheter eventually removed and replaced with
     a 9 French peel away sheath.  The guidewire and stilette was removed from the
     peel away sheath and the tunneled catheter was passed through the peel away
     into the right internal jugular vein.  The tip is in excellent position at the
     inferior edge of the previously placed superior vena cava stent at the orifice
     of the right internal jugular vein.  A chest film was taken to demonstrate th
     exact location.
     
     CONCLUSION:  Successful tunneling of a 7 French Hickman into the SVC.
